  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer12882959008551553298">A stranger walks out of a bar and is later found dead at the wheel of his car. The narrator creates the story of this man -- or, rather, two stories, based on the two personae that he has imagined. One of these is named Enderlin; the other, Gantenbein.<br/><br/>Originally published as A Wilderness of Mirrors.</span>

<div id="review_440912191" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/440912191" />
    <a title="Nihidea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13922802-nihidea"><img alt="Nihidea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351095729p2/13922802.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/440912191?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nihidea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nihidea" href="/user/show/13922802-nihidea">Nihidea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/15840737-mein-name-sei-gantenbein">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13922802-nihidea?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13922802-nihidea?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13922802-nihidea?shelf=german">german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13922802-nihidea?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440912191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11489139882405316456">Okay, now that I have finished the book for the second time, I feel up to writing a review about it. Now I feel I have halfway captured what is even going on. Or not going on. Because, let’s face it, 95% of what is happening in this book is not even happening. Okay?<br/><br/>Wait, first things first. This book is amazing. I shit you not. It fascinated me every time over when I opened it withing a few sentences I was just baffled. Frisch’s writing style is incredible, and he manages to convey so many emoti</span>
  <span id="freeText11489139882405316456" style="display:none">Okay, now that I have finished the book for the second time, I feel up to writing a review about it. Now I feel I have halfway captured what is even going on. Or not going on. Because, let’s face it, 95% of what is happening in this book is not even happening. Okay?<br /><br />Wait, first things first. This book is amazing. I shit you not. It fascinated me every time over when I opened it withing a few sentences I was just baffled. Frisch’s writing style is incredible, and he manages to convey so many emotions, so deep and unimaginable feelings in such an everyday language. None of the words he uses is overly sophisticated, but together they form an exquisite example of highly poetic literature. I can not stress enough how good this book is.<br />And that is even though virtually nothing happens.<br />It’s an amazing tale of fantasy and escapism, of searching for identity, of exploring life in only your mind, of sonder. Oh, so much sonder.<br /><br />There are so many layers. Honestly guys. Forget all about Inception. There is a fuckload of layers in this book and you might need a few times, just as I needed a few times and will probably need a few more to really grasp this book in its entirety, but guys, it’s SO worth it.<br /><br />I can not thank my Literature teacher from high school enough for recommending this to me. She, too, was as completely captivated by this book as I am now, and with this enthusiasm she got me to read it although I didn’t like Max Frisch. It completely changed my mind.<br /><br />This is a book that will occasionally make you laugh, occasionally bring you to the verge of tears, quite a few times present you with emotions you can relate to so much that it hurts, and always, always will it suck you completely into its world of absurdity, or confusion, of fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11489139882405316456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2085054391" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2085054391" />
    <a title="J.M. Hushour" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17463213-j-m-hushour"><img alt="J.M. Hushour" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442964894p2/17463213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2085054391?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.M. Hushour" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.M. Hushour" href="/user/show/17463213-j-m-hushour">J.M. Hushour</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2085054391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16383758455160654188">Frisch is one of those authors that you always run and try to convince people to read, but who is infuriatingly difficult to define. Thus, ultimately you fail to convince because you don't have a convenient pigeonhole to shove him into. That is part of his charm. Forgotten or at the least overlooked to a criminal degree, his musings on identity and the fictional layerings that are part and parcel, and almost obligatory, as part of being human in a world of ever-shifting parameters and definition</span>
  <span id="freeText16383758455160654188" style="display:none">Frisch is one of those authors that you always run and try to convince people to read, but who is infuriatingly difficult to define. Thus, ultimately you fail to convince because you don't have a convenient pigeonhole to shove him into. That is part of his charm. Forgotten or at the least overlooked to a criminal degree, his musings on identity and the fictional layerings that are part and parcel, and almost obligatory, as part of being human in a world of ever-shifting parameters and definition as to what they exactly mean, is more relevant than ever. Frisch himself described this book as: "The story isn't told as if a person could be identified by his factual behavior; let him betray himself in his fictions."<br />"Gantenbein" is a refreshing kind of narrative monster, where characters are subject to abrupt starts and stops, the narrative changed and veered, and the characters put through the existential wringer by the author who, by dint of being the author, gets a free pass to act sadistically on his characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16383758455160654188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33331112?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juliane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juliane" href="/user/show/1072178-juliane">Juliane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783518367865" href="/book/show/582732.Mein_Name_sei_Gantenbein">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072178-juliane?shelf=swiss">swiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072178-juliane?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072178-juliane?shelf=1960s">1960s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33331112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9956177938296986431">I have to admit, that this one is definitely my favourite book by Max Frisch. Gantenbein continues to explore the uneasy fascination with problems of personal identity, a topic which you can find in all of Max Frisch's novels. The narrative architecture of Gantenbein is manifestly chaotic. But that doesn't matter. The narrative perspective shifts periodically between the unnamed third person to any one of three named first person narrators, sometimes within a single sentence. I loved most the ro</span>
  <span id="freeText9956177938296986431" style="display:none">I have to admit, that this one is definitely my favourite book by Max Frisch. Gantenbein continues to explore the uneasy fascination with problems of personal identity, a topic which you can find in all of Max Frisch's novels. The narrative architecture of Gantenbein is manifestly chaotic. But that doesn't matter. The narrative perspective shifts periodically between the unnamed third person to any one of three named first person narrators, sometimes within a single sentence. I loved most the role of Gantenbein, who is opting for a existance in simulated (or fake) blindness to better watch his fellow passengers. Gantenbein believes, that also his fellow passengers are playing a special role and that they try to mislead him. Gantenbein is playing his part so well, that everyone is buying his story, but he has to be careful, always having his role in mind. Until the day, where he is getting out of his role...<br />Max Frisch's role playing is both misleading and fatal to love because it renders impossible the necessary adjustments and compromises involved in a constantly evolving relationship. <br />Absolutely recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9956177938296986431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4106804154724630548"><i>Mein Name seid Gantenbain</i> lacks the ironical, smart yet indifferent (gleichgültig) voice of the storyteller. It lacks the storytelling of <i>Homo Faber</i>, that which made me want to read more works of Frisch's in the first place.<br/><br/>I read this in German.<br/>I did not enjoy it, perhaps because I did not understand it.<br/>I liked <i>Homo Faber</i> much better.<br/><br/>I borrowed this book from a friend whose mother is Swiss.   <span id="freeText4106804154724630548" style="display:none"><i>Mein Name seid Gantenbain</i> lacks the ironical, smart yet indifferent (gleichgültig) voice of the storyteller. It lacks the storytelling of <i>Homo Faber</i>, that which made me want to read more works of Frisch's in the first place.<br /><br />I read this in German.<br />I did not enjoy it, perhaps because I did not understand it.<br />I liked <i>Homo Faber</i> much better.<br /><br />I borrowed this book from a friend whose mother is Swiss. She was overjoyed to have me borrowing books from her personal library (as there aren't many German speakers in Israel).<br />I remember also seeing there Süskind's Perfume, as well as many other interesting books... Maybe I'll have better luck next time...</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2024350203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10708301622341128682">This is a magnificent work. It is not written spontaneously, it is not created by writing free improvisation of fantasies, as it may seem at first glance. No, I think that every word in it is verified by author, like the perfect point of a sword. And every those word hits the target, it just hits. This is an excellent book, it's a classic of the 20th century.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39758715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13074362303952108439">I previously heard of Max Frisch mainly as a play writer but now I now he is also a good novelist.<br/>He is starting this novel by trying different stories. Then at some point he is focusing on two stories: the one of a man that is pretending to be blind and another one that has just received and invitation to Harvard. The second one is called Enderlin, but the first one does not seem to have a name. After he is telling the introduction of his story he says "Let my name be Gantenbein". I like this l</span>
  <span id="freeText13074362303952108439" style="display:none">I previously heard of Max Frisch mainly as a play writer but now I now he is also a good novelist.<br />He is starting this novel by trying different stories. Then at some point he is focusing on two stories: the one of a man that is pretending to be blind and another one that has just received and invitation to Harvard. The second one is called Enderlin, but the first one does not seem to have a name. After he is telling the introduction of his story he says "Let my name be Gantenbein". I like this literrary game and I hope to develope more.<br />I have finished reading this book and I am not so much impressed about it. I somehow expected the initial game to develop into a real plot. Instead of this the author is balancing between characters and stories and is never really sure about what he wants to write in this book. I am somewhat disapointed about this.<br />As a final remark it seems to be the kind of book that may be written by persons that have personality disorder. I might be wrong.<br />My copy of this book is in romanian.</span>

Actually, his blindness helps him to see himself and the others in a different light!). Of course, his gealousy guides his acts...And now I wonder...Was he just pretending to be blind?   <span id="freeText18244698803535943128" style="display:none">It was the first novel I read by Max Frisch and I must admit I became a fun. Very well written, with a bitter-sweet sense of humor, deals with the daily problems of an ”abnormal” couple (he pretends to be blind in order to have a better ”control” towards his marriage. Actually, his blindness helps him to see himself and the others in a different light!). Of course, his gealousy guides his acts...And now I wonder...Was he just pretending to be blind? Or was the gealousy the one who ended up by making him blind? <br />A very profound, touching and ”asking question” novel. <br />And - at last but not at least - an invitation to approach and ”to taste” this writer*s work!</span>

  <span id="freeText12313144822024046669" style="display:none">Like many others, I am going to re-read the book to understand all of its layers and multiple roles that are introduced to a reader. 5 stars already for the wonderful short stories that Gantenbein tells Kamilla. The idea of pretending blind is so simple, yet so powerful. And same goes to the writing style of Frisch - simple words, yet sharper than knife sometimes. <br />Can't wait for the next book - Stiller! </span>

<div id="review_1001853691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1001853691" />
    <a title="Dalel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8823630-dalel"><img alt="Dalel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408144923p2/8823630.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1001853691?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dalel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dalel" href="/user/show/8823630-dalel">Dalel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1001853691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1650502461023570834">I find this book quite interesting for an anti-novel. The way with which the narrator sways from one possible scenario to the other is very much like how the human brain functions in a dream, or daydream. The novel as a whole doesn't make much sense; there is no one precise and clear story, just fragments.<br/>On the other hand, I find the book unpleasantly long. By the time I have reached the last 50 pages, I've lost all interest in the characters and story/ stories.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

The language tends to be rather dry - the feature of all German-language writing authors probably, but generalizing is dangerous.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('c8cyjEW+u73XBx84P2HjPuJ1H6sb9fJs5C9FlAwndIPThwue81z+3Kj//Vg2P5EbF0zoU/DZpBJC8TWAuXgKmw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PR+K0eT8RWY+FXGaPSNEdeeO996lVQymt3yoLsI9FDGdX7PDUh4AB0Htk/o0fTZQErcAJk55WtgRotg6d2JqKQ==')})
  }

Yet his novel can also be seen as a plea for rigorous self-examination and an indictment of the intellectual hypocrisy of the period. Selbstkritisch gesteht er: »Das Ende haben wir nicht gut bestanden, beide nicht.« Noch über den schmerzvollen Bruch hinaus beziehen sie sich in ihren Werken aufeinander, geben sie in ihren Texten innerste Gefühle und Verwundungen preis.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6530.Max_Frisch">About Max Frisch</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/6530.Max_Frisch"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1223192970p3/6530.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/6530.Max_Frisch">Max Frisch
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
521
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10834148752630636612">Max Rudolph Frisch was born in 1911 in Zurich; the son of Franz Bruno Frisch (an architect) and Karolina Bettina Frisch (née Wildermuth). After studying at the Realgymnasium in Zurich, he enrolled at the University of Zurich in 1930 and began studying German literature, but had to abandon due to financial problems after the death of his father in 1932. Instead, he started working as a journalist a</span>
  <span id="freeText10834148752630636612" style="display:none">Max Rudolph Frisch was born in 1911 in Zurich; the son of Franz Bruno Frisch (an architect) and Karolina Bettina Frisch (née Wildermuth). After studying at the Realgymnasium in Zurich, he enrolled at the University of Zurich in 1930 and began studying German literature, but had to abandon due to financial problems after the death of his father in 1932. Instead, he started working as a journalist and columnist for the Neue Zürcher Zeitung (NZZ), one of the major newspapers in Switzerland. With the NZZ he would entertain a lifelong ambivalent love-hate relationship, for his own views were in stark contrast to the conservative views promulgated by this newspaper. In 1933 he travelled through eastern and south-eastern Europe, and in 1935 he visited Germany for the first time.<br /><br />From 1936 to 1941 he studied architecture at the ETH Zurich. His first and still best-known project was in 1942, when he won the invitation of tenders for the construction of a public swimming bath right in the middle of Zurich (the Letzigraben).<br /><br />In 1947, he met Bertolt Brecht in Zurich. In 1951, he was awarded a grant by the Rockefeller Trust and spent one year in the U.S. After 1955 he worked exclusively as a freelance writer. His experience of postwar Europe is vividly described in his Tagebuch (Diary) for 1946-1949; it contains the first drafts of later fictional works.<br /><br />During the 1950s and 1960s Frisch created some outstanding novels that explored problems of alienation and identity in modern societies. These are I'm Not Stiller (1954), Homo Faber (1957) and Wilderness of Mirrors/Gantenbein (1964). In addition, he wrote some highly intelligent political dramas, such as Andorra and The Fireraisers. He continued to publish extracts from his diaries. These included fragments from contemporary media reports, and paradoxical questionnaires, as well as personal reflections and reportage. he fell in love with a woman called Antonia Quick in 1969.<br /><br />Max Frisch died of cancer on April 4, 1991 in Zurich. Together with Friedrich Dürrenmatt, Max Frisch is considered one of the most influential Swiss writers of the 20th century. He was awarded an honorary degree by the University of Marburg, Germany, in 1962, Bard College (1980), the City University of New York (1982), the University of Birmingham (1984), and the TU Berlin (1987). He also won many important German literature prizes: the Georg-Büchner-Preis in 1958, the Friedenspreis des Deutschen Buchhandels in 1976, and the Heinrich-Heine-Preis in 1989. In 1965 he won the Jerusalem Prize for the Freedom of the Individual in Society.<br /><br />Some of the major themes in his work are the search or loss of one's identity; guilt and innocence (the spiritual crisis of the modern world after Nietzsche proclaimed that "God is dead"); technological omnipotence (the human belief that everything was possible and technology allowed humans to control everything) versus fate (especially in Homo faber); and also Switzerland's idealized self-image as a tolerant democracy based on consensus — criticizing that as illusion and portraying people (and especially the Swiss) as being scared by their own liberty and being preoccupied mainly with controlling every part of their life.<br /><br />Max Frisch was a political man, and many of his works make reference to (or, as in Jonas und sein Veteran, are centered around) political issues of the time.<br /><br />information was taken from<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Frisch">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Frisch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10834148752630636612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
